Merging a font with itself achieves nothing
When merging two CID keyed fonts, they must have the same Registry and Ordering, and the font being merged into (the mergee) must have a supplement which is at least as recent as the other's. Furthermore the mergee must have at least as many subfonts as the merger.

/usr/share/fontforge/fontforge
Neither FontForge nor iconv() supports your encoding (%s) we will pretend
 you asked for latin1 instead.
FontForge does not support your encoding (%s), it will try to use iconv()
 or it will pretend the local encoding is latin1
Failed to read OtherSubrs from %s
When FontForge starts up, it loads the user interface theme from
this file. Any changes will only take effect the next time you start FontForge.
Show splash screen on start-up
Typing a normal character in the glyph view window changes the window to look at that character
When double clicking on a character in the font view
open that character in a new window, otherwise
reuse an existing one.
The number of em-units by which an arrow key will move a selected point
Holding down the Shift key will speed up arrow key motion by this factor
When the mouse pointer is within this many pixels
of one of the various interesting features (baseline,
width, grid splines, etc.) the pointer will snap
to that feature.
When dragging points in the outline view a join may occur
(two open contours may connect at their endpoints). When
this is On a join will cause FontForge to stop moving the
selection (as if the user had released the mouse button).
This is handy if your fingers are inclined to wiggle a bit.
Figure out flex hints after every change
When generating a set of BDF fonts ask the user
to specify the screen resolution of the fonts
otherwise FontForge will guess depending on the pixel size.
Display rulers in the Outline Glyph View
If you wish to replace Adobe's OtherSubrs array (for Type1 fonts)
with an array of your own, set this to point to a file containing
a list of up to 14 PostScript subroutines. Each subroutine must
be preceded by a line starting with '%%%%' (any text before the
first '%%%%' line will be treated as an initial copyright notice).
The first three subroutines are for flex hints, the next for hint
substitution (this MUST be present), the 14th (or 13 as the
numbering actually starts with 0) is for counter hints.
The subroutines should not be enclosed in a [ ] pair.
Default encoding for
new fonts
The default size of the Em-Square in a newly created font.
Whether new fonts should contain splines of quadratic (truetype)
or cubic (postscript & opentype).
Use the FreeType rasterizer (when available)
to rasterize glyphs in the font view.
This generally results in better quality.
Whether fonts loaded from the disk should retain their splines
with the original order (quadratic or cubic), or whether the
splines should be converted to the default order for new fonts
(see NewFontsQuadratic).
When loading a truetype or opentype font which has both a unicode
and a CJK encoding table, use this flag to specify which
should be loaded for the font.
When loading a font in sfnt format (TrueType, OpenType, etc.),
ask the user to specify which cmap to use initially.
Enter a list of 4 letter table tags, separated by commas.
FontForge will make a binary copy of these tables when it
loads a True/OpenType font, and will output them (unchanged)
when it generates the font. Do not include table tags which
FontForge thinks it understands.
In the Outline View, the Shift key constrains motion to be parallel to the ItalicAngle rather than constraining it to be vertical.
When the user clicks in the editing window, round the location to the nearest integers.
The Edit->Join command will join points which are this close together
A value of 0 means they must be coincident
When copying glyphs from the font view, also copy the
glyphs' metadata (name, encoding, comment, etc).
The maximum number of Undoes/Redoes stored in a glyph
Changing the width of a glyph
changes the widths of all accented
glyphs based on it.
Changing the left side bearing
of a glyph adjusts the lbearing
of other references in all accented
glyphs based on it.
Instructions in a TrueType font refer to
points by number, so if you edit a glyph
in such a way that some points have different
numbers (add points, remove them, etc.) then
the instructions will be applied to the wrong
points with disasterous results.
  Normally FontForge will remove the instructions
if it detects that the points have been renumbered
in order to avoid the above problem. You may turn
this behavior off -- but be careful!
The percentage of an em by which an accent is offset from its base glyph in Build Accent
When placing grave and acute accents above letters, should
FontForge center them based on their full width, or
should it just center based on the lowest point
of the accent.
When centering an accent over a glyph, should the accent
be centered on the highest point(s) of the glyph,
or the middle of the glyph?
Use spacing accents (Unicode: 02C0-02FF) rather than
combining accents (Unicode: 0300-036F) when
building accented glyphs.
FontForge supports two different helper applications to do autotracing
 autotrace and potrace
If your system only has one it will use that one, if you have both
use this option to tell FontForge which to pick.
Extra arguments for configuring the autotrace program
(either autotrace or potrace)
Ask the user for autotrace arguments each time autotrace is invoked
Commands to pass to mf (metafont) program, the filename will follow these
Ask the user for mf commands each time mf is invoked
FontForge loads large images into the background of each glyph
prior to autotracing them. You may retain those
images to look at after mf processing is complete, or
remove them to save space
MetaFont (mf) generates lots of verbiage to stdout.
Most of the time I find it an annoyance but it is
important to see if something goes wrong.
Name used for foundry field in bdf
font generation
Name used for Vendor ID field in
ttf (OS/2 table) font generation.
Must be no more than 4 characters
FontForge will use this namelist when assigning
glyph names to code points in a new font.
Once upon a time, Adobe assigned PUA (public use area) encodings
for many stylistic variants of characters (small caps, old style
numerals, etc.). Adobe no longer believes this to be a good idea,
and recommends that these encodings be ignored.
 The assignments were originally made because most applications
could not handle OpenType features for accessing variants. Adobe
now believes that all apps that matter can now do so. Applications
like Word and OpenOffice still can't handle these features, so
 fontforge's default behavior is to ignore Adobe's current
recommendations.
Note: This does not affect figuring out unicode from the font's encoding,
it just controls determining unicode from a name.
Allow the full unicode character set in glyph names.
This does not conform to adobe's glyph name standard.
Such names should be for internal use only and
should NOT end up in production fonts.
If specified this should be a space separated list of integers each
less than 16777216 which uniquely identify your organization
FontForge will generate a random number for the final component.
AutoHint changed glyphs before generating a font
FontForge will place vertical or horizontal hints to describe the bounding boxes of suitable glyphs.
FontForge will place vertical or horizontal hints at the ends of diagonal stems.
FontForge will place vertical or horizontal hints at the intersections of diagonal stems.
FontForge will generate diagonal stem hints, which then can be used by the AutoInstr command.
MS has changed (in August 2006) the inner workings of their Indic shaping
engine, and to disambiguate this change has created a parallel set of script
tags (generally ending in '2') for Indic writing systems. If you are working
with the new system set this flag, if you are working with the old unset it.
(if you aren't doing Indic work, this flag is irrelevant).

Internal Error: 
BlueFuzz
Can't insert 'cvt'
Can't insert 'prep'
Can't insert 'fpgm'
Can't instruct this glyph
The ball terminal with a key point at %.3f,%.3f
appears to be incorrectly linked to the %s stem
<%.3f, %.3f>
There already exists a 'cvt' table, perhaps legacy. FontForge can use it, but can't make any assumptions on values stored there, so generated instructions will be of lower quality. If legacy hinting is to be scrapped, it is suggested to clear the `cvt` and repeat autoinstructing. 
There exists a 'prep' code incompatible with FontForge's. It can't be guaranteed it will work well. It is suggested to allow FontForge to insert its code and then append user's own.
There exists a 'fpgm' code that seems incompatible with FontForge's. Instructions generated will be of lower quality. If legacy hinting is to be scrapped, it is suggested to clear the `fpgm` and repeat autoinstructing. It will be then possible to append user's code to FontForge's 'fpgm', but due to possible future updates, it is extremely advised to use high numbers for user's functions.
TrueType does not support mixed references and contours.
If you want instructions for %.30s you should either:
 * Unlink the reference(s)
 * Copy the inline contours into their own (unencoded
    glyph) and make a reference to that.
We're about to crash.
We miscalculated the glyph's instruction set length
When processing TTF instructions (hinting) of %s
TrueType does not support references which
are scaled by more than 200%%.  But %1$.30s
has been in %2$.30s. Any instructions
added would be meaningless.

%% <font> <encoding> font_remap <font>	; from the cookbook
/font_remap { reencodedict begin
  /newfont basefont  maxlength dict def
    exch dup dup /FID ne exch /Encoding ne and
	{ exch newfont 3 1 roll put }
  newfont /Encoding newencoding put
  /foo newfont definefont	%%Leave on stack
/n_show { moveto show } bind def
